17:33
C.J. Lovell
COMPUTER ADVICE REQUESTED

Hi! I have divided my hard drive (a SSD) into two partitions (C - 120 gb and D - 3890 gb). Recently, I was doing a conversation of a video into a different format (wmv to mp4) and I found out that my C drive had run out of memory.

I couldn't understand it because the OS (Windows 10) should occupy at the most 50 gb.

Anyways I only had "megabytes" left before I used the drive compression option. (I had already used the "disk cleaner utility and it only free up 1/2 a gigabyte).

What should I do to resolve this problem? Should I compress the drive (which from what I've read will result in slower performance of my computer)?

Should I buy a bigger SSD drive (HDD are much slower and I don't want a lag in performance)?

Please give me some advice. (I have about an intermediate understanding of IT subjects, so feel free to use technical explanations to help me with my problem. (I am just a few years out of practice ;-) )
AT

17:54
Nikita Borodulin
I think, this is not about resizing or compressing partitions. Assuming that the process of video conversion finished successfully, there still might be some temporary files on your C: drive left by software you used to convert your video. So first thing, I'd advice you to check what exactly takes so much space on your C: drive. Chances are it's something you don't need:)
